<div id="review_222158772" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222158772" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2465351-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324174664p2/2465351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222158772?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/2465351-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=genre-bending">genre-bending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=revelation-space">revelation-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=the-innocent-get-screwed">the-innocent-get-screwed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465351-ian?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222158772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17979565356344922306">The family's godfather sat back in his plush leather recliner and calmly ordered the hit, like the man who was about to be murdered was nothing more than a bug to be squashed …<br/><br/>The crack sniper squinted through his gun's sight, aligning the target's forehead in the crosshairs, and pulled the trigger with no second thoughts or remorse …<br/><br/>The muck and grime of the city's underworld didn't alarm him at all, as he trudged through the rain-flooded streets in search of his prey …<br/><br/>Come one, come all, see t</span>
  <span id="freeText17979565356344922306" style="display:none">The family's godfather sat back in his plush leather recliner and calmly ordered the hit, like the man who was about to be murdered was nothing more than a bug to be squashed …<br /><br />The crack sniper squinted through his gun's sight, aligning the target's forehead in the crosshairs, and pulled the trigger with no second thoughts or remorse …<br /><br />The muck and grime of the city's underworld didn't alarm him at all, as he trudged through the rain-flooded streets in search of his prey …<br /><br />Come one, come all, see the bazaar! Eat the spiced meat! Meet the best doctor in the slum, he only kills one in twenty! …<br /><br />He loved her, loved her deeply; she was the most precious thing in his universe, the only one who knew what he was capable of and yet loved him anyway …<br /><br />The generational colony ship slid along its preset course to Journey's End, surrounded only by the absolute silence and darkness of deep interstellar space …<br /><br />There is a ghost ship following us …<br /><br />There is a ghost following us …<br /><br />It was a dark and stormy night …<br /><br />I am what is known as an unreliable narrator …<br /><br />History is written by the victors …<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />Several of my GR friends have read <i>Chasm City</i> and had mixed reactions ranging from "it sucks" to "it's just okay." Well they're wrong. I think they couldn't handle <i>Chasm City</i> (… you can't <i>HANDLE</i> the truth!!! …). It's darkness, it's depth, it's muck overwhelmed them. This book is <i>dirty good</i>.<br /><br />I've now read all of Alastair Reynolds' books set in his <i>Revelation Space</i> universe. I began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/89195.The_Prefect__Revelation_Space__Standalone_" title="The Prefect (Revelation Space, Standalone) by Alastair Reynolds" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prefect</a>
</i> and, as I said in my review, it was not snazzy book but it was exceptionally well executed. <i>Chasm City</i> was both snazzy <i>and</i> well executed. Okay, maybe "snazzy" isn't the right word … "oozy" is probably better. I know it sounds gross, and I suppose that's partially the meaning I intend to convey, but I also mean that <i>Chasm City</i> oozes darkness and human desperation, and I further mean that the setting—Chasm City itself—oozes around you while your read, displacing your warm and comfortable wealthy Western surroundings. For in <i>Chasm City</i>, Reynolds has given us a dripping wet, sticky, seedy, smelly shithole of a place to set a story … a city covered in a layer of literal and figurative slime … a city which has no laws except the law of the strong and the weak, the law of the very rich and the very poor… a city inhabited by buildings that have reshaped themselves according to their own arcane will … and the buildings inhabited by people that scrape the bottom of the barrel of human experience and are grateful for the handful of filth they find. In <i>Chasm City</i>, Reynolds dives headfirst into the sci-fi noir experience … and drags us with him.<br /><br />And what makes <i>Chasm City</i> (the book) so excellent is that the sci-fi noir experience doesn't end at the rim of Chasm City (the city). The book takes us on an interstellar voyage aboard a generational ship under the grip of petty personal power struggles and paranoid conspiracy theories, both real and imagined, the crew making bargains with the devil amidst the literal darkness outside and the figurative darkness inside. The book takes us on a hunt on the planet Sky's Edge, where society has been torn apart by a centuries-long war with no end in sight, where—unless you are very wealthy—your life is sure to feel the unpleasant impact of the war's constant hammering.<br /><br /><i>Chasm City</i> is a book of deliberate hyperbole in which Reynolds showcases some of the worst of what humanity has to offer, filled with extreme examples and nasty caricatures that rise to the level of wry satire and sardonic cheese. Normally that sort of thing doesn't sit well with me but it works much better in a dark context than in a humorous or other lighter context. In <i>Chasm City</i> Reynolds seems to be paying homage to cheesy who-dun-its, plot-twisty detective novels and overwrought crime thrillers. In this respect <i>Chasm City</i> doesn't seem to take itself too seriously, an important element of getting the reader to accept what Reynolds is doing.<br /><br />Reynolds uses some inventive methods, or at least clever twists on older methods, for revealing both the characters' pasts and the history of the worlds in which the story is set. A character recovering from amnesia certainly is a tried and true method of revealing someone's past, but Reynolds manages to make the amnesia fit into the story in a logical way; the amnesia doesn't come across as a contrived excuse. The more inventive method Reynolds uses is an "indoctrinal virus"—which is pretty much what it sounds like. One of the main characters contracts this virus, which implants the memories of a revered historical figure, thereby revealing key historical facts.<br /><br /><i>Chasm City</i> is creative and it's in your face. <i>Chasm City</i> is dark and dirty. <i>Chasm City</i> is juicy and chewy and it burns your throat on the way down. <i>Chasm City</i> is … Chasm City.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17979565356344922306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8588910133383434087"><br/><br/>"How long would you have to live; how much good would you have to do, to compensate for one act of pure evil you'd committed as a younger man?"<br/><br/>Redemption. It seems to be one of Reynold's favorite themes. It was prevelant in the Revelation Space series, and it takes <br/>center stage in Chasm City. <br/> <br/>It's normal for Alastair's novels to push the 500 page mark, but unlike other works I've read in this genre, his stories <br/>are lean and mean. This is the leanest and meanest story I've read of his. Although </span>
  <span id="freeText8588910133383434087" style="display:none"><br /><br />"How long would you have to live; how much good would you have to do, to compensate for one act of pure evil you'd committed as a younger man?"<br /><br />Redemption. It seems to be one of Reynold's favorite themes. It was prevelant in the Revelation Space series, and it takes <br />center stage in Chasm City. <br /> <br />It's normal for Alastair's novels to push the 500 page mark, but unlike other works I've read in this genre, his stories <br />are lean and mean. This is the leanest and meanest story I've read of his. Although this novel clocks in at almost 700 <br />pages, Reynolds does not waste time, and there is very little extreaneous material to be found here. <br /><br />After I read the 3 Revelation Space books, this book sat on my shelf for 2 years because I feared that a Reynolds story <br />being confined to a single city would feel claustrophobic. I was really wrong. To my delight, we quickly find out that we <br />are going to be splitting time not only on Chasm City, but also on Sky's Edge, and on the generation ships sent to colonize <br />this world orbiting 61 Cygni. <br /><br />Those parts were probably my favorite, because I absolutely love the sociological implications of being part of a flotilla of 6 ships travelling at sublight speed for 150 years, each ship basically an <br />independant island in and of itself, regardless (or in spite) of the fact that they are headed to the same destination. <br /><br />Let's just say the results are not pretty, but to be expected when you consider our sometimes primitive nature. <br /><br />Why is this flotilla's destination name changed from Journey's End to Sky's Edge? The answer is probably one of the coolest <br />parts of this novel; the stunning action that was committed for that name to stick decades after colonization is <br />at the very crux of why Sky Haussmann is in such desperate need for redemption. <br /><br />Its a mind blowing thrill ride all the way through. </span>

<div id="review_53443171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53443171" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480285828p2/1199525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53443171?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=scifi-future-speculative-fict">scifi-future-speculative-fict</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53443171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7936014183906252365">I read this because Alistair Reynolds is my teenage son's favourite author. Although it is sometimes labelled as Revelation Space book 2, he reckoned this was the best book and has the advantage of being readable as a standalone story. <br/><br/>Although you could summarise it as a long chase story of hunter and hunted, it is a complex and well-written page turner (and there are quite a lot of pages), the main theme of which is the nature of identity and the effects of various ways of changing it (e.g. bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7936014183906252365" style="display:none">I read this because Alistair Reynolds is my teenage son's favourite author. Although it is sometimes labelled as Revelation Space book 2, he reckoned this was the best book and has the advantage of being readable as a standalone story. <br /><br />Although you could summarise it as a long chase story of hunter and hunted, it is a complex and well-written page turner (and there are quite a lot of pages), the main theme of which is the nature of identity and the effects of various ways of changing it (e.g. body mods, memory implants, nanotech, DNA manipulation, immortality, reefersleep to travel through time and space). <br /><br />There are three main stories, set in different times and places and it swaps between them without ever being confusing. The main one concerns Tanner Mirabel's attempt to track down and kill Argent Reivich for revenge. This involves leaving his home planet of Sky's Edge and travelling to Chasm City on Yellowstone, once rich and technologically advanced, but now devastated by a nanotech virus. The gap between the poor who live in the Mulch and the rich in the Canopy is extreme and the idle rich liven their lives in dangerous ways. Previously, Mirabel was an ex soldier, hired as private security/bodyguard for Cahuella, a rich arms dealer with many enemies. Cahuella, and one hunting expedition in particular, is the second thread. The third strand follows Sky Haussman and is set a couple of hundred years earlier. Sky grows up as crew on one of a flotilla of space ships sent to colonise a new world. There are rivalries within and between ships, including deaths. Obviously as the book progresses, the links between these different stories gradually emerge. <br /><br />The science is plausible and invariably explained as a natural part of the story, though occasionally he kept me waiting for the explanation rather longer than I wanted. Reynolds has a good feel for characters' inner thoughts and emotions (something that is not always true of sci fi) and manages to make each distinct without resorting to gimmicky dialects and non-standard spelling, although they somehow seem a little flat at the same time. He's also very good at helping the reader visualise all the strange worlds in glorious detail - at times I could "see" it as if I was watching a film. <br /><br />There were a few sections that were a little clichéd, especially the ending, which felt a little rushed after nearly 600 leisurely pages, but overall, I thought it was a very good read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7936014183906252365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755334377?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=biopunk">biopunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=transhumanism">transhumanism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755334377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12394810554351459689">There's something very important attached to modern, well-crafted space-opera. It's not precisely the way new and old tech drives the boundaries of plot, nor is it the very common feel of jaded semi-immortals gripping onto their lives in fascist drama. It's something hidden, an underlay of expectations that successfully build so much momentum that the text screams like a runaway train and it doesn't matter how much inane and crazy plot-twists crop up, because you're just left holding on to the r</span>
  <span id="freeText12394810554351459689" style="display:none">There's something very important attached to modern, well-crafted space-opera. It's not precisely the way new and old tech drives the boundaries of plot, nor is it the very common feel of jaded semi-immortals gripping onto their lives in fascist drama. It's something hidden, an underlay of expectations that successfully build so much momentum that the text screams like a runaway train and it doesn't matter how much inane and crazy plot-twists crop up, because you're just left holding on to the ride.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, this novel wasn't particularly fast paced, but it did maintain a solid clip. I found myself somewhat rooting for the other trying to take over his mind long before the twists made it super plausible as well as inevitable. The only real issue I wanted to make was in the person he had originally began as, since there just wasn't enough presence or emotional immediacy, despite the whole reason for the multiple revenge scenarios. That persona was already lost by the time he knew it was lost, and so there wasn't any immediacy or consequence to it, and I thought that might have been a great opportunity to turn a good book into a good gut-wrenching book.<br /><br />I thought it was quite fun, and I think I'll be recommending Mr. Reynolds widely.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12394810554351459689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5804542408865862214">It's a great sci-fi book, maybe one of the best of this century. There are three main points, why it is so good.<br/><br/>1. First is a plot. It is interesting, captivating and consistant, but this isn't so important. Composition is. There are three story lines, from the first glance almost unconnected. But when they finally merge, you can see, how good Reynolds is. This composition is kind of quirky, but it makes the whole picture very beautiful.<br/><br/>2. This is hard sci-fi. Reynolds is a physicist, so his fic</span>
  <span id="freeText5804542408865862214" style="display:none">It's a great sci-fi book, maybe one of the best of this century. There are three main points, why it is so good.<br /><br />1. First is a plot. It is interesting, captivating and consistant, but this isn't so important. Composition is. There are three story lines, from the first glance almost unconnected. But when they finally merge, you can see, how good Reynolds is. This composition is kind of quirky, but it makes the whole picture very beautiful.<br /><br />2. This is hard sci-fi. Reynolds is a physicist, so his fiction is realistic. There are no faster-than-light space travels; beam weapons, i mean of small arms, do not blow up targets or kill instantly, unles some vital organs are hit etc. Although there are some moments i do not agree with, as a whole, from the point of view of natural sciences it is mostly realistic. But strange thing, this book is more realistic from the point of view of logic, psychology, and social sciences. And this i like very much.<br /><br />3. And the most beautiful part - the atmosphere. Virgin jungles of Sky's Edge, small crews at large ships of flotilla drifting in a deep space, and urban ambient of this mesmerizingly nice megalopolis Chasm City. All this is described so vividly that you can feel this deep solitude at the spaceship or weirdness and unsafety of the city. Could someone tell me how to get to Epsilon Eridani system? LOL</span>
  <a data-text-id="5804542408865862214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3072123379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3072123379" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99853253-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602426860p2/99853253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3072123379?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/99853253-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who has read the earlier books in the series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99853253-william?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3072123379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11699055746152281035">Chasm City is the third prequel to Alistair Reynolds' "Revelation Space" series, but it is not a sequel to The Prefect, and Elysium Fire. In addition to the main series and prequels, many characters and places are present in "Beyond the Aquila Rift: The Best of Alistair Reynolds", Pushing Ice (which I have not yet read), Galactic North (which I have not yet read), Diamond Dogs, and the short story Open and Shut (which I have also not read). As for the reading order, my recommendation would be th</span>
  <span id="freeText11699055746152281035" style="display:none">Chasm City is the third prequel to Alistair Reynolds' "Revelation Space" series, but it is not a sequel to The Prefect, and Elysium Fire. In addition to the main series and prequels, many characters and places are present in "Beyond the Aquila Rift: The Best of Alistair Reynolds", Pushing Ice (which I have not yet read), Galactic North (which I have not yet read), Diamond Dogs, and the short story Open and Shut (which I have also not read). As for the reading order, my recommendation would be the following. This is how I read them, and it was a very satisfying experience:<br /><br />1. Beyond the Aquila Rift: The Best of Alistair Reynolds<br />2. Revelation Space<br />3. Redemption Ark<br />4. Absolution Gap<br />5. The Prefect (AKA Aurora Rising)<br />6. Elysium Fire<br />7. Chasm City<br /><br />8. House of Suns - This takes place six million years in the future of the RS universe. The Abigail Gentian story is first mentioned in the short story "Thousandth Night" from Beyond The Aquila Rift, but does not share timeline continuity, which sounds odd, but it works. Both are fantastic reads, just ignore the lore discrepancies. Don't let it ruin your fun. :) Reynolds himself has commented on this and basically said the same.<br /><br />I consider Chasm City the best book in the series, but they are all fantastic. I also don't think it would really be possible to fully appreciate Chasm City without the foundation built from earlier books. <br /><br />Anyone reading this has probably read at least six books in the series, so there's really no point in urging anyone to continue. Potential readers are almost certainly hooked, and only death would stop them from finishing the series. My only recommendation would be "don't die before you finish the series" because it goes out with a bang.<br /><br />Thanks again for the great reading Al. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11699055746152281035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2418948338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2418948338" />
    <a title="Chris Berko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13125862-chris-berko"><img alt="Chris Berko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501820241p2/13125862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2418948338?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Berko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Berko" href="/user/show/13125862-chris-berko">Chris Berko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2418948338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer463350618956302042">This works on so many different levels. It is an excellent sci-fi yarn with awesome ideas, it is a Memento-like who-the-fuck-is-who mystery, and at it's basest level it is an old fashioned revenge tale; and I loved every minute of it. This is my second Reynolds book after the original Revelation Space novel and while I loved both books, this was easier to read and flowed more smoothly. The gigantic concepts and shit are still there but the writing is more mature and confident. Nowadays this book</span>
  <span id="freeText463350618956302042" style="display:none">This works on so many different levels. It is an excellent sci-fi yarn with awesome ideas, it is a Memento-like who-the-fuck-is-who mystery, and at it's basest level it is an old fashioned revenge tale; and I loved every minute of it. This is my second Reynolds book after the original Revelation Space novel and while I loved both books, this was easier to read and flowed more smoothly. The gigantic concepts and shit are still there but the writing is more mature and confident. Nowadays this book would be split into two in order to make more money and all so I miss the days of these 800 page behemoths and not having to wait a year to finish a story originally meant for one book because of greedy publishers. To wrap it up, this is very cinematic in its delivery and it really does keep you guessing until the very last page. Five enthusiastic thumbs up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="463350618956302042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_615594430" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615594430" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162390-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525386186p2/4162390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615594430?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4162390-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=epic-science-fiction">epic-science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615594430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12989470829555584059">Once again Alastair Reynolds has me all over the place with my thoughts on his books. There are parts of this story that I throughly enjoyed and would happily give four stars and then there are great rafts of it that I found dull and couldn't wait for the chapter to end. Thus three stars is the result. <br/><br/>Chasm City has some Revelation Space theme to it, but you couldn't be faulted in thinking that there were two Alastair Reynolds in the authoring world. This story is told in such a different way t</span>
  <span id="freeText12989470829555584059" style="display:none">Once again Alastair Reynolds has me all over the place with my thoughts on his books. There are parts of this story that I throughly enjoyed and would happily give four stars and then there are great rafts of it that I found dull and couldn't wait for the chapter to end. Thus three stars is the result. <br /><br />Chasm City has some Revelation Space theme to it, but you couldn't be faulted in thinking that there were two Alastair Reynolds in the authoring world. This story is told in such a different way that it is hard to credit I had just finished reading the same writer. <br />Chasm City is told in three story arcs that curve to a convergence to give you a final understanding of wtf this is all about. <br /><br />The three stories are all interesting and two of the arcs are historical to the first as characters begin to gain their memories back of past traumatic events. There are whole bunch of familiar themes with this, including a copy of The Running Man theme and whilst I was reasonably enjoying the different stories I really really didn't like the main character...at all. It was almost as if the character had sat in his cubicle and read every Stainless Steel Rat novel he could find. His lines were corny and the delivery awful. I admit this may have something to do with the way the book was read by the narrator. <br /><br />This review is coming over somewhat negative and I guess that is indicative to the things that grate you as opposed to the parts that went well. Overall, the story was interesting and there were lots of parts that had my attention. But I didn't love it and never once found myself not being able to put it down. <br /><br />I am going to persevere with Reynolds as I have been told, I should like his work, given my tastes. I am trying Redemption Arc next and hope to find that place where I start to enjoy the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12989470829555584059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_4259667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4259667" />
    <a title="Swaps55" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251287-swaps55"><img alt="Swaps55" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376517361p2/251287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4259667?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Swaps55" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Swaps55" href="/user/show/251287-swaps55">Swaps55</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Sci-fi fans, sci-fi writers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=best-books-ever">best-books-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=alastair-reynolds">alastair-reynolds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4259667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7145349438604931074">This is the first alastair Reynolds book I read, and I was so blown off my ass I couldn't think straight for a few days. This guy has the perfect toolkit for writing science fiction: a background in astrophysics, an amazing imagination, a strong sense of character and a compelling plot with a deserving ending. What attracts me most to his writing is his uncanny grasp of human nature and human behavior, and what it would evolve into when projected into the future, when technological advancements </span>
  <span id="freeText7145349438604931074" style="display:none">This is the first alastair Reynolds book I read, and I was so blown off my ass I couldn't think straight for a few days. This guy has the perfect toolkit for writing science fiction: a background in astrophysics, an amazing imagination, a strong sense of character and a compelling plot with a deserving ending. What attracts me most to his writing is his uncanny grasp of human nature and human behavior, and what it would evolve into when projected into the future, when technological advancements are as mind-boggling to us as the internet would be to the cave man. <br /><br />Of all his books, I maintain that this one is the most dedicated to the characters, and has the most self-contained plot. Though very dense and extremely satisfying, it does not have the overwhelming, epic scope that his Inhibitor trilogy does (this book takes place in the Inhibitor universe as a standalone piece, although reading it will provide a lot of helpful insight into the trilogy). The focus is a lot narrower, which is what I think allows him to dwell more on the societal construct that I found so fascinating. <br /><br />While his exposition gets to be extensive, and the technobabble overwhelming, through those things he establishes an unmistakable command of his material, something more science fiction writers need to establish. If you want a lesson in pushing boundaries, this is it. If you read science fiction, are a fan of space opera, and/or write in this genre, this book should be required reading. It honest to God changed the way I look at science fiction. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7145349438604931074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12690574199278621316">I really wish GoodReads did half stars - because I liked this one more than just a "3 rating" would suggest. For me, 4 and 5 star books are things that I would like to read again, they are books I loved, and books I would recommend to others. This is definitely a book I'd recommend to someone that liked sci-fi, but it isn't going to make my favorites list or be something I'll read again.<br/><br/> Chasm City was a good story, but it was slow to get going. There really isn't one likeable character in the e</span>
  <span id="freeText12690574199278621316" style="display:none">I really wish GoodReads did half stars - because I liked this one more than just a "3 rating" would suggest. For me, 4 and 5 star books are things that I would like to read again, they are books I loved, and books I would recommend to others. This is definitely a book I'd recommend to someone that liked sci-fi, but it isn't going to make my favorites list or be something I'll read again.<br /><br /> Chasm City was a good story, but it was slow to get going. There really isn't one likeable character in the entire book, and in parts it got too overly descriptive for me. That being said, the plot was interesting. I was invested in what was happening to the characters (despicable as they were). Maybe I wouldn't like it if I hadn't already read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12007.Use_of_Weapons__Culture___3_" title="Use of Weapons (Culture, #3) by Iain M. Banks" rel="nofollow noopener">Use of Weapons</a> - I was constantly comparing the two in my mind. <br /><br />So 3.5 stars because I liked this book a lot, but I didn't love it.<br /><br />PS - I was up late reading this one and then had dreams about snakes. sigh.</span>

<div id="review_91058408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91058408" />
    <a title="MadProfessah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2116192-madprofessah"><img alt="MadProfessah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482687972p2/2116192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91058408?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MadProfessah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MadProfessah" href="/user/show/2116192-madprofessah">MadProfessah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who live Leviathan Wakes or Judas Unchained</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2116192-madprofessah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91058408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2133146757116370808">British science fiction master <b>Alastair Reynolds</b> has very quickly become one of my favorite authors and <a href='http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0441010644?ie=UTF8&tag=themadprolec-20&linkCode=as2&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=0441010644' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Chasm City</i>
</a> is a big part of that. Although it is not formally in the <i>Revelation Space</i> trilogy of <i><a href='http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Revelation Space</a>, <a href='http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds_21.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Redemption Ark</a> </i>and <i>Absolution Gap</i>, it is set in the same universe as those other books, like <i>
  <a href='http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/09/book-review-alastair-reynolds-prefect.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Prefect</a>
</i> and his short story collection <i>Galactic North.</i><br/><br/>Specifically, Chasm City is located on the planet Yellowstone, which once featured the most advanced human civilization in</span>
  <span id="freeText2133146757116370808" style="display:none">British science fiction master <b>Alastair Reynolds</b> has very quickly become one of my favorite authors and <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0441010644?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=themadprolec-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0441010644" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Chasm City</i>
</a> is a big part of that. Although it is not formally in the <i>Revelation Space</i> trilogy of <i><a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelation Space</a>, <a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds_21.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Redemption Ark</a> </i>and <i>Absolution Gap</i>, it is set in the same universe as those other books, like <i>
  <a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/09/book-review-alastair-reynolds-prefect.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prefect</a>
</i> and his short story collection <i>Galactic North.</i><br /><br />Specifically, Chasm City is located on the planet Yellowstone, which once featured the most advanced human civilization in Reynolds' <i>
  <a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelation Space</a>
</i> universe; the planet and its environs are mentioned frequently in <i>
  <a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Revelation Space</a>
</i> and <i>
  <a href="http://buckmire.blogspot.com/2010/10/book-review-alastair-reynolds_21.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Redemption Ark</a>
</i>.<br /><br />The main character of <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0441010644?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=themadprolec-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0441010644" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Chasm City</i>
</a> is Tanner Mirabel, or at least we the reader <i>think</i> it is. One of the themes in Reynolds' work that I have noticed is the idea that the narrator doesn't always know their own identity. In other words, the threat of subversion of one's individual identity is always a possibility. Tanner arrives on Yellowstone from another planet called Sky's Edge in order to kill Argent Reivich, whom he believes killed the woman he loved (who just happened to have been the wife of the crime boss Cahuella who hired Tanner to be his chief of security). This storyline appears to be a pretty straightforward revenge tale.<br /><br />The second, more intriguing story is about Sky Haussman, the original colonist of Tanner's home planet Sky's Edge, who in the intervening centuries since the planet's colonization has become revered as a near God-like figure by some but a Machiavellian mass-murderer by others. Tanner has been infected with a bizarre virus which causes the infected to bleed stigmatically from the palm and to dream obsessively about the life story of Sky Haussman and the sad, bizarre tale of how Sky's Edge was colonized.<br /><br />There are multiple other subplots, which are also well-written and fascinating. One of the most memorable involves a bizarre extra-terrestrial  creature which is part plant and part reptile called a hamadryad which Cahuella is obsessed with capturing and confining in his private zoo/garden. Another subplot involves a subculture in Chasm City which revolves around a particular drug called "dream fuel." This dangerous substance allows users to avoid the devastating effects of the Melding Plague (a nanotech virus which destroys all machines at a cellular level, including nanomachines that most advanced humans possess during this era and which shows up in the other <i>Revelation Space</i> novels).<br /><br /><i><a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0441010644?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=themadprolec-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0441010644" rel="nofollow noopener">Chasm City</a> </i>is the most ambitious and intricately plotted of Reynolds novels, and, in my opinion, the most successful. The threads come together in a surprising way. I thought I had figured out the secret twist about two-thirds through the novel but there was a twist on the twist which completely floored me.<br /><br />Any lover of well-conceived speculative fiction who has an appreciation for other genres (especially hard-boiled detective fiction) will not be disappointed by taking the time to read <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0441010644?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=themadprolec-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0441010644" rel="nofollow noopener">Chasm City</a>.<br /><br />Author: Alastair Reynolds.<br />Title: Chasm City.<br />Length: 704 pages.<br />Publisher: Ace.<br />Date: May 27, 2003.<br /><br />PLOT: A+.<br />IMAGERY: A.<br />IMPACT: A.<br />WRITING: A+.<br /><br />OVERALL GRADE: A+/A (4.15/4.0).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2133146757116370808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review91058408">

<div id="review_816646426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816646426" />
    <a title="Mark Hebwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25942645-mark-hebwood"><img alt="Mark Hebwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513522869p2/25942645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816646426?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Hebwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Hebwood" href="/user/show/25942645-mark-hebwood">Mark Hebwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816646426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1168062035374692234">Well. I must say I am impressed. It is not often that I find something truly new, and original. That is not in any way meant to be a glib statement - I think all of us who like to read can say that we have encountered many plot twists that are of a similar nature, many clever narrative modes which yet feel as if they pertain to a common class, many beautifully crafted and unique characters.<br/><br/>And yet, In <i>Chasm</i> City, Alastair served up something truly new (at least for me) and managed to deliver a r</span>
  <span id="freeText1168062035374692234" style="display:none">Well. I must say I am impressed. It is not often that I find something truly new, and original. That is not in any way meant to be a glib statement - I think all of us who like to read can say that we have encountered many plot twists that are of a similar nature, many clever narrative modes which yet feel as if they pertain to a common class, many beautifully crafted and unique characters.<br /><br />And yet, In <i>Chasm</i> City, Alastair served up something truly new (at least for me) and managed to deliver a reading sensation I have never had before. Two thirds through the novel, he does something with the narrative mode that turned me inside out, and the effect was not diminished for the fact that it was not entirely unpredictable. I saw it coming, but when it <i>did</i> actually happen, I was still stunned. I felt betrayed, disorientated, dislocated. My fictional world had been turned upside down with <i>one</i> word, with <i>one</i> stroke of the pen.<br /><br />But I will stop now before I say too much. It dismays me that I cannot tell you more, but if I did, I'd ruin a seismic shift in reading experience for you. So I can only say that Alastair delivers another complex, intelligent, and highly original read. These reads do not always work for me, for example I was unable to warm to <i>Revelation Space</i>, but even when they don't, there is no doubt that Alastair is a bright guy, who manages to blend astrophysical knowledge and writing skill into a richly textured fictional rendition of transhumanism.<br /><br />And at the heart of it, Chasm City tells a very simple story. Banal even. It is no more than the old theme of "boy avenges the murder of his loved one". But this story is told through one of the most intricately interwoven narrative modes I have ever encountered. This, in the end, is what made this novel stand out for me - the contrast between story and form.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="1168062035374692234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2573082272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2975625120382750280">Chasm City is proof that Alastair Reynolds has a dark side. And it is wonderful.<br/><br/>This is a revenge tale following a bad ass, morally ambivalent (yet perhaps ultimately redeemable?) mercenary pursuing his prey across ruined, deformed worlds devastated by war and a catastrophic nanobot plague. During his pursuit, he slowly unravels, revealing a murky, disturbing past.<br/><br/>The story is smart and quick paced, and the world building superb. Reynolds paints a brooding, menacing landscape, brimming with mind</span>
  <span id="freeText2975625120382750280" style="display:none">Chasm City is proof that Alastair Reynolds has a dark side. And it is wonderful.<br /><br />This is a revenge tale following a bad ass, morally ambivalent (yet perhaps ultimately redeemable?) mercenary pursuing his prey across ruined, deformed worlds devastated by war and a catastrophic nanobot plague. During his pursuit, he slowly unravels, revealing a murky, disturbing past.<br /><br />The story is smart and quick paced, and the world building superb. Reynolds paints a brooding, menacing landscape, brimming with mind blowing cyberpunk motifs based on runaway nanotech, cyerbnetics and genetic engineering.<br /><br />"As for the fourth, she figured in my plans, which is why she wasn't currently emptying her soul into a puddle of warm rain."</span>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DiUa7fEKdcxz2RJrC081hdUMMq8255TIlPWAFIkMixCAUabb5xwIwkmDzEX+IGNwLwPfrYfaZRCZ4Bgr7pAouw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7UTzbiwWr9mffY4XpRcqRwI1alfuhbpKYSPb7o1WKMRjME9YOgDS16UnUDlQeHyy+DqHVV+4S5JsNkPR6sqLbw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15415443330944942316">I'm Al, now a Goodreads author. I used to be a space scientist, and now I'm a writer, although for a time the two careers ran in parallel. I started off publishing short stories in the British SF magazine Interzone in the early 90s, then eventually branched into novels. I write about a novel a year and try to write a few short stories as well. Some of my books and stories are set in a consistent f</span>
  <span id="freeText15415443330944942316" style="display:none">I'm Al, now a Goodreads author. I used to be a space scientist, and now I'm a writer, although for a time the two careers ran in parallel. I started off publishing short stories in the British SF magazine Interzone in the early 90s, then eventually branched into novels. I write about a novel a year and try to write a few short stories as well. Some of my books and stories are set in a consistent future named after Revelation Space, the first novel, but I've done a lot of other things as well and I like to keep things fresh between books. <br /><br />I was born in Wales, but raised in Cornwall, and then spent time in the north of England and Scotland. I moved to the Netherlands to continue my science career and stayed there for a very long time, before eventually returning to Wales.<br /><br />In my spare time I am a very keen runner, and I also enjoying hill-walking, birdwatching, horse-riding, guitar and model-making. I also dabble with paints now and then. I met my wife in the Netherlands through a mutual interest in climbing and we married back in Wales. We live surrounded by hills, woods and wildlife, and not too much excitement.</span>

        $('bookCover_89184').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_89184').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_89184').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
